potentially fatal...", "body": "Minnesota-based Hormel Foods Sales LLC issued a recall for two Planters products produced at one of its facilities and distributed to five states in the southeast portion of the US because they could cause fatal infections.\n\nHormel produced the contaminated Honey Roasted Peanuts and Deluxe Lightly Salted Mixed Nuts for Planters at one of its facilities before distributing them to Publix warehouses in Florida, Georgia, Alabama and North Carolina as well as Dollar Tree warehouses in South Carolina and Georgia.\n\nAfter producing and distributing the products in April, Hormel discovered the packaged contents could be contaminated with listeria monocytogenes.\n\nThe organism listeria monocytogenes can cause serious and sometimes fatal infections in young children, elderly people and others who have weakened immune systems.\n\nHealthy individuals who consume the organism could suffer short-term symptoms like high fever, severe headache, stiffness, nausea, abdominal pain and diarrhea, according to the voluntarily issued recall.\n\nAdditionally, listeria infections can cause pregnant women to have miscarriages or stillbirths.\n\nThe product being recalled is limited to 4-ounce packages of Planters Honey Roasted Peanuts and 8.75-ounce cans of Planters Deluxe Lightly Salted Mixed Nuts.\n\nCans of Deluxe Lightly Salted Mixed Nuts have a \"Best if Used By Date\" on the bottom as well as a UPC code on the side.\n\nThe UPC code for Honey Roasted Peanuts in question is 2900002097 with a best-by date of April 11, 2025.\n\nFor deluxe Lightly Salted Mixed Nuts, the UPC code in question is 2900001621 and the best-by date is April 5, 2026.\n\nHormel said these are the only products in the recall.\n\nThe company also said there have not been any reports of anyone getting sick from the recalled products and all retailers affected have been notified.\n\nAnyone in possession of the affected products is urged not to consume the nuts but instead either discard them or return them to the store where they were purchased for a replacement or full refund.\n\n\"Our commitment to food safety remains our utmost priority,\" Hormel said. \"A full investigation is currently underway to determine the potential source of the contamination.\"\n\nFor questions or concerns about the recall, consumers can contact Hormel Foods customer relations at This is a precautionary measure as any Listeria monocytogenes infection may cause serious and fatal health conditions.\n\nAs stated in the recall announcement, healthy individuals who ingested the said dangerous organism could experience short-term symptoms such as severe headache, nausea, diarrhea, abdominal pain, high fever, and stiffness.\n\nIt could be fatal for the elderly, young children, and those with weak immune systems. Fatal Contamination", "body": "Minnesota-based Hormel Foods Sales LLC issued a recall for two Planters products produced at one of its facilities and distributed to five states in the U.S. because of the potential to cause fatal infections.\n\nHormel produced the contaminated Honey Roasted Peanuts and Deluxe Lightly Salted Mixed Nuts for Planters at one of its main facilities before distributing them to Publix warehouses in Alabama, Florida, Georgia and North Carolina as well as Dollar Tree warehouses in Georgia and South Carolina.\n\nAfter producing the potential fatal products in April, Hormel discovered that the packaged contents could be contaminated with listeria monocytogenes.\n\nThe organism listeria monocytogenes can cause serious and sometimes fatal infections in young children, elderly people and others who have weakened immune systems.\n\nAccording to the recall, healthy individuals who consume the product could potentially suffer short-term symptoms like high-fever, abdominal pain, nausea, diarrhea and stiffness.\n\nAdditionally, listeria infections can cause pregnant women to have miscarriages or stillbirths.\n\nThe product being recalled is limited to 4-ounce packages of Planters Honey Roasted Peanuts and 8.75 ounce cans of Planters Deluxe Lightly Salted Mixed Nuts.\n\nFurthermore, cans of Deluxe Lightly Salted Mixed Nuts have a \"Best if Used By Date\" on the bottom as well as a UPC code on the side.\n\nThe UPC code for Honey Roasted Peanuts in question is 2900002097 with a best-by date of April 11, 2025.\n\nFor deluxe Lightly Salted Mixed Nuts, the UPC code in turmoil is 2900001621 and the best-by date is April 5, 2026.\n\nAccording to Hormel, these are the only products in the recall.\n\nMeanwhile, the company also stated there have not been any reports of anyone getting sick from the recalled products and retailers supplying the items have been notified.\n\nConsumers who are in possession of the affected products are urged not to consume the nuts but return the item to the store to receive a full refund.\n\n\"Our commitment to food safety remains our utmost priority,\" Hormel said. \"A full investigation is currently underway to determine the potential source of the contamination.\"\n\nFor questions or concerns about the recall, consumers can contact Hormel Foods customer relations at 800-523-4635.\n\nStay informed! A full investigation is currently under way to determine the potential source of the contamination,\" the company stated.\n\nThe recall is limited to two items, according to Hormel Foods: 4-ounce packages of Planters Honey Roasted Peanuts and 8.75-ounce cans of Planters Deluxe Lightly Salted Mixed Nuts.\n\nAs of time of publication, the company said there had been \"no reports of illness related to this recall,\" adding that \"all retailers that received the affected product have been properly notified.\"\n\nA representative for Hormel Foods told ABC News the company had \"no additional updates beyond the [recall] notice at this time.\"\n\nImpacted products can be identified by their \"Best if Used By\" date and UPC code.\n\nRecalled Honey Roasted Peanuts bear the UPC code 2026.\n\n\"The 'Best if Used By Date' is located on the bottom of the Deluxe Lightly Salted Mixed Nuts can and the UPC code is located on the side of the can,\" Hormel Foods stated in its recall announcement.\n\nClick here for additional information and photos of the affected products.\n\nNo other varieties of Planters branded products were included in this recall.\n\nAccording to Hormel Foods, the recall impacts only \"two retailers in five states.\"\n\n\"The products were shipped to Publix distribution warehouses in Florida, Georgia, Alabama and North Carolina and to Dollar Tree distribution warehouses in South Carolina and Georgia,\" the company said Friday.\n\nIt added, \"If a consumer has this product, they can discard the product or return it to the store where purchased for an exchange or full refund.\"\n\nCustomers with questions can contact Hormel Foods Customer Relations via the email portal on the company's website, via chat at https://www.planters.com or by phone at 1-800-523-4635, Monday through Friday, 8-11 a.m. and 2-4 p.m. CT, excluding holidays.\n\nListeria monocytogenes is an organism that can cause severe illness \"when the bacteria spread beyond the gut to other parts of the body\" after a person consumes contaminated food, according to the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention. Those at higher risk include pregnant people, those aged 65 or older, or anyone who has a weakened immune system, the CDC states.\n\n\"For people who are pregnant, Listeria can cause pregnancy loss, premature birth, or a life-threatening infection in their newborn,\" the agency states. \"For people who are 65 years or older or who have a weakened immune system, Listeria often results in [severe illness that may lead to] hospitalization and sometimes death.\"\n\nOther people can be infected with listeria, but rarely become seriously ill, according to the FDA. The company said the affected products came from one of its facilities in April.\n\nThe company said the recall only includes certain products that were shipped to Publix warehouses in Florida, Georgia, Alabama and North Carolina, and to Dollar Tree warehouses in South Carolina and Georgia.\n\nThe company said that the recall includes 4-ounce packages of Planters Honey Roasted Peanuts that have \"best if used by\" date of April 11, 2025 and a package UPC code of 2900002097. The recall also includes 8.75 ounce cans of Planters Deluxe Lightly Salted Mixed Nuts that have with \"best if used by\" date of April 5, 2026 and a package UPC code of 2900001621.\n\nHormel Foods noted that no other Planters products are affected by the recall and that there have been no reported illnesses in connection to the recall so far. Those who have the recalled products should toss them or return them to the retailer for a refund or exchange, the company said.\n\nAccording to the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (CDC), a listeria infection is most likely to sicken those who are pregnant, newborns, those 65 and older or those with weakened immune systems.\n\nA listeria infection in pregnant women can cause stillbirth, miscarriages, premature delivery or an infection of the newborn, according to the CDC. Listeria infection can cause miscarriages, stillbirths and preterm labor among pregnant women.\n\nOthers can be infected with listeria, but it's rare for them to become very ill: In healthy people, symptoms include fever, stiff neck, headache and flu-like symptoms, according to the CDC.\n\nThe recall affects 4-ounce packages of Planters Honey Roasted Peanuts with a \"best if used by\" date of April 11, 2025, and a package UPC code of 2900002097. It also affects 8.75-ounce cans of Planters Deluxe Lightly Salted Mixed Nuts with a \"best if used by\" date of April 5, 2026, and a package UPC code of 2900001621 on the side of the can.\n\nNo other products or packaging sizes are included in the recall, Minnesota-based Hormel Foods said.\n\nCustomers should discard the nuts or return them to the store where they purchased them for an exchange, the company added.\n\nThe CDC estimates that 1,600 people get sick from listeria each year and that about 260 die, making listeria the third leading cause of death from food poisoning in the United States.\n\nHormel Foods said in a notice posted on the Food and Drug Administration's website that \"commitment to food safety remains our utmost priority\" and that \"a full investigation\" is Healthy people may suffer symptoms such as high fever, severe headache, stiffness, nausea, abdominal pain and diarrhea, Hormel noted.\n\nThe recalled products were shipped to Dollar Tree distribution Listeria also commonly affects adults 65 years and older and people with weakened immune systems.\n\n\"Healthy individuals may suffer only short-term symptoms such as high fever, severe headache, What is Listeria", "body": "E.Coli, metal and even a dead bat have been found in recalled food. In fact, food recalls are increasing. Yet, that might actually be a good sign. Here's why.\n\nNo one has reported getting sick, but two types of Planters nuts sold in Florida Publix locations have been recalled over concerns of potential Listeria contamination.\n\nHormel Foods Sales LLC is voluntarily recalling specific lots of 8.75 oz cans of Planters Deluxe Lightly Salted Mixed Nuts and 4 oz packages of Planters Honey Roasted Peanuts, according to a release from the company and the FDA Friday.\n\nListeria monocytogenes can cause \"serious and sometimes fatal infections in young children, frail or elderly people, and others with weakened immune systems,\" the release said.\n\nThe recalled items were produced at one of Hormel Foods's facilities in April, according to the company's release, and were shipped to Publix distribution warehouses in Florida, Georgia, Alabama and North Carolina and to Dollar Tree distribution warehouses in South Carolina and Georgia. The company does not know the potential source of the contamination but is investigating.\n\n'There have been no reports of illness related to this recall to date,\" Hormel Foods said, \"and all retailers that received the affected product have been properly notified.\"\n\n\"No other sizes, varieties, or other packaging configurations of Planters brand products are included in this recall,\" the company said.\n\nWhat do I do if I bought some of the recalled Planters nuts?\n\nIf you bought either of these items, you can throw them out or return them to the store where you bought them for a full refund, Publix said in a release.\n\nIf consumers have questions, Hormel Foods said they may contact Foods Customer Relations via email here, via chat at https://www.planters.com/ or at 1-800-523-4635, Monday-Friday, 8-11 a.m. and 2 -4 p.m. Central Time, excluding holidays.\n\nWhat is Listeria?\n\nListeria monocytogenes are bacteria that can infect people with something called listeriosis that is usually mild, according to the CDC, but can spread beyond the intestines to cause fetal loss or newborn death in pregnant people and sepsis (infection of the bloodstream), meningitis or encephalitis (infection of the brain).\n\nInfection during pregnancy results in fetal loss in about 20% of cases and newborn death in about 3% of cases, the CDC said. Listeria also commonly affects adults 65 years and older and people with weakened immune systems.\n\n\"Healthy individuals may suffer only short-term symptoms such as high fever, severe headache, stiffness, nausea, abdominal pain, and diarrhea,\" Hormel Foods said in the release.\n\nThe CDC estimates that Listeria is the third leading cause of death from foodborne illness in the United {"uri": "2024-05-346885074", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-06", "time": "19:31:53", "dateTime": "2024-05-06T19:31:53Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-06T19:27:45Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6470588445663452, "url": "https://www.cnn.com/2024/05/06/health/planters-nuts-recall-listeria/index.html", "title": "Some Planters nut products recalled over possible listeria contamination", "body": "Two Planters nut products have been recalled due to possible contamination with the bacteria that causes listeria.\n\nCNN --\n\nHormel Foods has recalled two Planters products - peanuts and mixed nuts - due to possible contamination with the bacteria that causes listeria, according to an announcement from the company that was posted by the US Food and Drug Administration on Friday.\n\nThe two recalled products - 4-ounce packages of honey roasted peanuts and 8.75-ounce cans of deluxe lightly salted mixed nuts - were distributed to retailers in five Southern states: Publix warehouses in Florida, Georgia, Alabama and North Carolina and Dollar Tree warehouses in South Carolina and Georgia.\n\nOne of two products recalled by Hormel Foods. From Hormel Foods\n\nThe peanuts have a \"best if used by\" date of April 11, 2025, and the mixed nuts have a \"best if used by\" date of April 5, 2026.\n\nAs of Friday, there were no reported illnesses related to this recall. However, the company says it is conducting an investigation to identify the potential source of the contamination.\n\nConsumers who purchased these products are urged to throw them away or return them to the store where purchased for an exchange or full refund.\n\nListeria monocytogenes bacteria can cause a serious infection, though the symptoms may vary by the type of infection and person affected, according to the US Centers for Disease Control and Prevention.\n\nWhile often mild, symptoms of intestinal illness can include diarrhea and vomiting that develop within a day of eating contaminated food and last for a few days. Intestinal illness can spread, leading to a more severe illness with flu-like symptoms - such as muscle aches, fatigue and fever - that usually start about two weeks after eating contaminated food.\n\nGet CNN Health's weekly newsletter\n\nSign up here to get The Results Are In with Dr. Sanjay Gupta every Tuesday from the CNN Health team.\n\nListeria is most dangerous to pregnant women and newborns, seniors and others with weakened immune systems. Illness may appear mild in pregnant people but could lead to miscarriage, stillbirth, premature delivery or life-threatening infection of the newborn.\n\nAbout 1,600 people get listeriosis each year in the United States, causing about 260 deaths, according to the CDC.\n\nListeria can be detected through a lab test. at two retailers in five states due to possible contamination with potentially deadly listeria doesn't surprise Northeastern University food policy expert Darin Detwiler.\n\nHe says peanuts are at particular risk of being contaminated with the food-borne bacteria that causes listeria due to the way they are harvested, handled and stored.\n\nBut Detwiler, an associate teaching professor, says recalls could be reduced if producers delayed shipping peanut products until they received the results of safety testing for contaminants such as listeria.\n\nAs it is, he says, the products are shipped off to distribution centers and then to stores, where unsuspecting customers may purchase peanuts and other nuts that later may be subject to recalls.\n\nThe stakes are high.\n\nHealthy people may suffer the temporary discomfort of a high fever, severe headache, stillness, nausea, stomach pain and diarrhea, the FDA says.\n\nBut infections from listeria monocytogenes can be serious and even fatal in young children, frail or elderly people and those with weakened immune systems.\n\nIt is also known to cause stillbirths and miscarriages, Detwiler says.\n\nThe FDA says Hormel is voluntarily recalling 4-ounce packages of Planters Honey Roasted Peanuts and 8.75-ounce cans of Planters Deluxe Lightly Salted Mixed Nuts produced at one of its facilities in April and shipped to Publix distribution warehouses in Florida, Georgia, Alabama and North Carolina, and to Dollar Tree distribution warehouses in South Carolina and Georgia.\n\nThe FDA site lists the UPC and use by dates of the recalled products so consumers can discard or return them -- if they haven't already consumed them.\n\n\"Not every peanut (in the recall) is contaminated,\" Detwiler says.\n\nBut he says the recall means \"a sample from a lot or batch number was taken and it was shown to be contaminated.\"\n\nPeanuts are easily contaminated by the pathogens that cause listeria and also salmonella, Detwiler says.\n\n\"They are harvested and handled in various environments where they can come into contact with contaminated soil and contaminated water. Even minimal exposure can lead to the introduction of pathogens.\"\n\n\"A lot of these peanuts are stored in massive mountains\" where they may come into contact with animal droppings, he said.\n\n\"Most nuts go through various processes -- shelling, roasting, packaging -- so there are many stages where contamination may occur. There could be contamination of the processing facilities and equipment,\" Detwiler says.\n\nAnd since many of the peanut and nut products are eaten raw, \"there's no kill step to kill these pathogens.\"\n\n\"We've had multiple outbreaks with peanuts,\" including one about 15 years ago that resulted in more than 700 known illnesses and nine deaths, Detwiler says.", "source": {"uri": However, the company says it is conducting an investigation to identify the potential source of the contamination.\n\nConsumers who purchased these products are urged to throw them away or return them to the store where purchased for an exchange or full refund.\n\nListeria monocytogenes bacteria can cause a serious infection, though the symptoms may vary by the type of infection and person affected, according to the US Centers for Disease Control and Prevention.\n\nWhile often mild, symptoms of intestinal illness can include diarrhea and vomiting that develop within a day of eating contaminated food and last for a few days. Intestinal illness can spread, leading to a more severe illness with flu-like symptoms - such as muscle aches, fatigue and fever - that usually start about two weeks after eating contaminated food.\n\nListeria is most dangerous to pregnant women and newborns, seniors and others with weakened immune systems. Illness may appear mild in pregnant people but could lead to miscarriage, stillbirth, premature delivery or life-threatening infection of the newborn.\n\nAbout 1,600 people get listeriosis each year in the United States, causing about 260 deaths, according to the CDC.\n\nListeria can be detected through a lab test. Most people recover without treatment, but more serious cases can be treated with an antibiotic.\n\nThe-CNN-Wire\n\n\u2122 & \u00a9 2024 Cable News Network, Inc., a Warner Bros. Discovery Company. {"uri": "8114144216", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-06", "time": "16:35:53", "dateTime": "2024-05-06T16:35:53Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-06T16:34:48Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.5254902243614197, "url": "https://www.theepochtimes.com/us/planters-nuts-recalled-due-to-potentially-fatal-listeria-infection-concerns-5644613", "title": "Planters Nuts Recalled Due to Potentially Fatal Listeria Infection Concerns", "body": "1,600 people get sick from the infection annually, with around 260 individuals dying, the CDC said.\n\nPlanters branded nut products have been recalled amid concerns about microbial infection that can be fatal for children and cause miscarriages among pregnant women, according to the U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA).\n\nThe products are being pulled from the market as they have the potential to be contaminated by Listeria monocytogenes, \"an organism that can cause serious and sometimes fatal infections in young children, frail or elderly people, and others with weakened immune systems.\"\n\n\"Healthy individuals may suffer only short-term symptoms such as high fever, severe headache, stiffness, nausea, abdominal pain, and diarrhea. Listeria infection can cause miscarriages and stillbirths among pregnant women.\"\n\nThe universal product code (UPC) for Honey Roasted Peanuts is 2900002097, with a \"Best if Used By Date\" of April 11, 2025. The Deluxe Lightly Salted Mixed Nuts has a UPC of 2900001621 and a \"Best if Used By Date\" of April 5, 2026.\n\nThe recall affects two retailers in five U.S. states, with items shipped to Dollar Tree distribution warehouses in South Carolina and Georgia, as well as to Publix distribution warehouses in Florida, Georgia, Alabama, and North Carolina.\n\n\"There have been no reports of illness related to this recall to date, and all retailers that received the affected product have been properly notified,\" according to the FDA notice.\n\nThe company advised Americans who have bought the product to discard it or return it to the store for an exchange or full refund. Images of the product can be found on the FDA notice webpage.\n\n\"People who have an allergy or severe sensitivity to peanuts run the risk of serious or life-threatening allergic reaction if they consume these products,\" the recall notice stated.\n\nThe agency estimates that 1,600 people get sick from listeria infections in the country every year, with roughly 260 individuals dying.\n\nPeople who are at greater risk of infection are pregnant women and their newborns, individuals 65 years of age or older, and people with weakened immune systems. While other individuals can be infected with listeria, \"they rarely become seriously ill,\" the CDC noted.\n\nAmong pregnant women, symptoms can include fever and flu-like symptoms such as fatigue and muscle aches. Other people may exhibit additional symptoms like headaches, stiff neck, confusion, loss of balance, and seizures.\n\nPregnant women who have invasive listeriosis may only show mild symptoms, with some females never having symptoms. Infection during pregnancy can lead to stillbirth, miscarriage, premature delivery, or life-threatening infection of the newborn.\n\nFor non-pregnant individuals, symptoms of invasive listeriosis can be \"severe,\" the CDC said while noting that almost one in 20 such individuals with the condition die.\n\nIndividuals carrying the invasive version of the illness are treated with antibiotics. Most people with intestinal illness recover from the condition without antibiotic treatment. However, antibiotics may be required for people who are very ill or at risk of becoming very ill.\n\nThe CDC identified queso fresco and cotija cheese made by a company called Rizo-Lopez Foods as being responsible for the 2024 outbreak.\n\n\"To slow down or prevent the growth of L. monocytogenes, set the refrigerator to 40 degrees Fahrenheit (4 degrees Celsius), and the freezer to 0 degrees Fahrenheit (-18 degrees Celsius).\"\n\nIf consumers think some food items may be contaminated with Listeria monocytogenes, the agency advised them to wash the insides of the refrigerator as well as cutting boards, countertops, utensils, and any other items that may have come into contact with the food.\n\nThese surfaces then need to be sanitized with a solution of one tablespoon of chlorine bleach to one gallon of hot water.\n\nFinally, the surfaces must be dried using a paper towel or clean cloth, the FDA stated.", "source": {"uri": "theepochtimes.com", "dataType": "news", "title":
